<th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Uyghur_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Uyghur Cyrillic alphabet">Siril Yëziqi</a></th>
<td>Җуңго Коммунистик Партийə</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Zhongwen.svg/40px-Zhongwen.svg.png" width="40" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Zhongwen.svg/60px-Zhongwen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Zhongwen.svg/80px-Zhongwen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="60" data-file-height="30" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> text.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(East_Asian)" title="Help:Multilingual support (East Asian)">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character" class="mw-redirect">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_character" title="Chinese character" class="mw-redirect">Chinese characters</a>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Communist Party of China</b> (<b>CPC</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>a<span>]</span></a></sup> is the founding and ruling <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC). The CPC is the sole governing party of China, although it coexists alongside 8 other legal parties that make up the <a href="/wiki/United_Front_(China)" title="United Front (China)" class="mw-redirect">United Front</a>. It was founded in 1921, chiefly by <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li_Dazhao" title="Li Dazhao">Li Dazhao</a>. The party grew quickly, and by 1949 the CPC had driven the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_government" title="Nationalist government">government</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">10-year civil war</a>, thus leading to the establishment of the People's Republic of China. The CPC is currently the world's second largest political party with a membership of 87.79 million as of 2015.</p>
<p>The CPC is, officially, organized on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">democratic centralism</a>, a principle conceived by <a href="/wiki/Russian_people" title="Russian people" class="mw-redirect">Russian</a> <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> theoretician <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> which entails democratic and open discussion on policy on the condition of unity in upholding the agreed upon policies. The highest body of the CPC is the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="National Congress of the Communist Party of China">National Congress</a>, convened every fifth year. When the National Congress is not in session, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">Central Committee</a> is the highest body, but since the body meets normally only once a year, most duties and responsibilities are vested in the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of China">Politburo</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo Standing Committee of the Communist Party of China">Standing Committee</a>. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="List of leaders of the Communist Party of China" class="mw-redirect">party's leader</a> holds the offices of <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of China">General Secretary</a> (responsible for civilian party duties), <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Central_Military_Commission" title="Chairman of the Central Military Commission">Chairman of the Central Military Commission</a> (CMC) (responsible for military affairs) and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="President of the People's Republic of China">state president</a> (a largely ceremonial position). Through these posts the party leader is the country's <a href="/wiki/Paramount_leader" title="Paramount leader">paramount leader</a>. The current party leader is <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>, elected at the <a href="/wiki/18th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="18th National Congress of the Communist Party of China">18th National Congress</a> (held in 2012).</p>
<p>The CPC is still committed to <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist thought</a> and continue to participate in the <a href="/wiki/International_Meeting_of_Communist_and_Workers%27_Parties" title="International Meeting of Communist and Workers' Parties">International Meeting of Communist and Workers' Parties</a> each year. According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Constitution of the Communist Party of China">party constitution</a> the CPC adheres to <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxism–Leninism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Mao Zedong Thought</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_Chinese_characteristics" title="Socialism with Chinese characteristics">socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping_Theory" title="Deng Xiaoping Theory">Deng Xiaoping Theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Three_Represents" title="Three Represents">Three Represents</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Outlook_on_Development" title="Scientific Outlook on Development">Scientific Outlook on Development</a>. The official explanation for China's <a href="/wiki/Reform_and_opening_up" title="Reform and opening up" class="mw-redirect">economic reforms</a> is that the country is in the <a href="/wiki/Primary_stage_of_socialism" title="Primary stage of socialism">primary stage of socialism</a>, a developmental stage similar to the <a href="/wiki/Capitalist_mode_of_production_(Marxist_theory)" title="Capitalist mode of production (Marxist theory)">capitalist mode of production</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> established under <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_market_economy" title="Socialist market economy">socialist market economy</a>, the current economic system, on the basis that "Practice is the Sole Criterion for the Truth" (i.e. the planned economy was deemed inefficient).</p>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">collapse of Eastern European communist regimes</a> in 1989–1990 and the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991, the CPC has emphasized its party-to-party relations with the ruling parties of the remaining <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist states</a>. While the CPC still maintains party-to-party relations with non-ruling communist parties around the world, it has since the 1980s established relations with several non-communist parties, most notably with ruling parties of one-party states (whatever their ideology), dominant parties in democratic systems (whatever their ideology), and <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democratic</a> parties.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="History of the Communist Party of China">History of the Communist Party of China</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_and_early_history_.281921.E2.80.9327.29">Founding and early history (1921–27)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding and early history (1921–27)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The CPC has its origins in the <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> of 1919, during which radical ideologies like <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_China" title="Anarchism in China">anarchism</a> gained traction among Chinese intellectuals.<sup id="cite_ref-XinhuaCPChistory_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XinhuaCPChistory-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Li Dazhao was the first leading Chinese intellectual who publicly supported <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199126_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199126-4"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In contrast to Chen Duxiu, Li did not renounce participation in the affairs of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" title="Republic of China (1912–49)">Republic of China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199127_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199127-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Both of them regarded the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in Russia as groundbreaking, believing it to herald a new era for oppressed countries everywhere.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199127_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199127-5"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC was modeled on <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>'s theory of a <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_party" title="Vanguard party" class="mw-redirect">vanguard party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199134.E2.80.9338_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199134.E2.80.9338-6"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Study circles were, according to <a href="/wiki/Cai_Hesen" title="Cai Hesen">Cai Hesen</a>, "the rudiments [of our party]".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199138_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199138-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Several study circles were established during the <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">New Culture Movement</a>, but "by 1920 skepticism about their suitability as vehicles for reform had become widespread."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199144_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_de_Ven199144-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1st_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="1st National Congress of the Communist Party of China">founding National Congress</a> of the CPC was held on 23–31 July 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> While it was originally planned to be held in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_French_Concession" title="Shanghai French Concession">Shanghai French Concession</a>, police officers interrupted the meeting on 3 July.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of that, the congress was moved to a tourist boat on <a href="/wiki/South_Lake_(Jiaxing)" title="South Lake (Jiaxing)">South Lake</a> in Jiaxing, Zhejiang province.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Only 12 delegates attended the congress, with neither Li nor Chen being able to attend.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Chen sent a personal representative to attend the congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The resolutions of the congress called for the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Communist_party" title="Communist party">communist party</a> (as a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern" class="mw-redirect">Communist International</a>) and elected Chen as its leader.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/180px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png" width="180" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/270px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/360px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="229" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flag of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People.27s_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The communists dominated the left wing of the KMT, a party organized on Leninist lines, struggling for power with the party's right wing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram196684.2C_89_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram196684.2C_89-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> When KMT leader <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> died in March 1925, he was succeeded by a rightist, <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, who initiated moves to marginalize the position of the communists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram196684.2C_89_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram196684.2C_89-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Fresh from the success of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a> to overthrow the warlords, Chiang Kai-shek turned on the communists, who by now numbered in the tens of thousands across China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeigon200242_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeigon200242-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Ignoring the orders of the Wuhan-based KMT government, he marched on Shanghai, a city controlled by communist militias. Although the communists welcomed Chiang's arrival, he turned on them, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_massacre_of_1927" title="Shanghai massacre of 1927">massacring 5000</a> with the aid of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Gang" title="Green Gang">Green Gang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeigon200242_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeigon200242-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram1966106_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram1966106-13"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197661.E2.80.9362_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197661.E2.80.9362-14"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Chiang's army then marched on Wuhan, but was prevented from taking the city by CPC General <a href="/wiki/Ye_Ting" title="Ye Ting">Ye Ting</a> and his troops.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram1966112_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram1966112-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Chiang's allies also attacked communists; in Beijing, 19 leading communists were killed by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zuolin" title="Zhang Zuolin">Zhang Zuolin</a>, while in Changsha, He Jian's forces machine gunned hundreds of peasant militiamen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram1966106.E2.80.93109.2C_112.E2.80.93113_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram1966106.E2.80.93109.2C_112.E2.80.93113-16"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197662_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197662-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> That May, tens of thousands of communists and their sympathisers were killed by nationalists, with the CPC losing approximately 15,000 of its 25,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197662_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197662-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The CPC continued supporting the Wuhan KMT government,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197662_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197662-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> but on 15 July 1927 the Wuhan government expelled all communists from the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197663_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197663-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC reacted by founding the Workers' and Peasants' Red Army of China, better known as the "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People.27s_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Red Army</a>", to battle the KMT. A battalion led by General <a href="/wiki/Zhu_De" title="Zhu De">Zhu De</a> was ordered to take the city of <a href="/wiki/Nanchang" title="Nanchang">Nanchang</a> on 1 August 1927 in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Nanchang_Uprising" title="Nanchang Uprising">Nanchang Uprising</a>; initially successful, they were forced into retreat after five days, marching south to <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">Shantou</a>, and from there being driven into the wilderness of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197663_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197663-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> was appointed commander-in-chief of the Red Army, and led four regiments against Changsha in the <a href="/wiki/Autumn_Harvest_Uprising" title="Autumn Harvest Uprising">Autumn Harvest Uprising</a>, hoping to spark peasant uprisings across Hunan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197664_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197664-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> His plan was to attack the KMT-held city from three directions on 9 September, but the Fourth Regiment deserted to the KMT cause, attacking the Third Regiment. Mao's army made it to Changsha, but could not take it; by 15 September, he accepted defeat, with 1000 survivors marching east to the <a href="/wiki/Jinggang_Mountains" title="Jinggang Mountains">Jinggang Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter197664_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter197664-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram1966122.E2.80.93125_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram1966122.E2.80.93125-20"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeigon200246.E2.80.9347_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeigon200246.E2.80.9347-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_Civil_War_and_World_War_II_.281927.E2.80.9349.29">Chinese Civil War and World War II (1927–49)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Chinese Civil War and World War II (1927–49)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a></div>
<p>The near-destruction of the CPC's urban organizational apparatus led to institutional changes within the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The party adopted democratic centralism, a way to organize revolutionary parties, and established a Politburo (functioned as the standing committee of the Central Committee).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The result was increased centralization of power within the party .<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> At every-level of the party this was duplicated, with standing committees now in effective control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> After Chen Duxiu's dismissal, <a href="/wiki/Li_Lisan" title="Li Lisan">Li Lisan</a> was able to assume <i>de facto</i> control of the party organization by 1929–30.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Li Lisan's leadership was a failure, and by the end of it, the CPC was on the brink of destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern" class="mw-redirect">Comintern</a> became involved, and by late-1930, his powers had been taken away.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1935 Mao had become the party's informal leader, with <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Wentian" title="Zhang Wentian">Zhang Wentian</a>, the formal head of the party, serving as his informal deputies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The conflict with the KMT led to the reorganization of the Red Army, with power now centralized in the leadership through the creation of CPC political departments charged with supervising the army.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199272_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199272-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> caused a pause in the conflict between the CPC and the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992370_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992370-23"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_United_Front" title="Second United Front">Second United Front</a> was established between the CPC and the KMT to tackle the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992354_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992354-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> While the front formally existed until 1945, all collaboration between the two parties had ended by 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992354_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992354-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite their formal alliance, the CPC used the opportunity to expand and carve out independent bases of operations to prepare for the coming war with the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992355_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992355-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1939 the KMT began to restrict CPC expansion within China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992355_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992355-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> This led to frequent clashes between CPC and KMT forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992355_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992355-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> It did not take long before the situation were deescalated, since none of the parties considered a civil war an option at this time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992355_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992355-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, by 1943 the CPC was again actively expanding its territory at the expense of the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992355_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992355-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg/220px-Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg/330px-Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f2/Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg 2x" data-file-width="414" data-file-height="320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mao_proclaiming_the_establishment_of_the_PRC_in_1949.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mao declared the establishment of the People's Republic of China on 1 October 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1945 until 1949, the war had been reduced to two parties; the CPC and the KMT.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> This period lasted through four stages; the first was from August 1945 (when the Japanese surrendered) to June 1946 (when the peace talks between the CPC and the KMT ended).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1945, the KMT had three-times more soldiers under its command than the CPC, and because of it, it looked early on like it was winning.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> With the cooperation of the Americans and the Japanese, the KMT was able to retake major parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> However, KMT rule over the reconquested territories would prove unpopular because of endemic corruption within the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this advantage, the KMT, with 2 million more troops than the CPC, failed to reconquer the rural territories which made up the CPC's stronghold.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Around the same time, the CPC launched an invasion of <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, where they were given assistance by the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The second stage, lasting from July 1946 to June 1947, saw KMT extend its control over major cities, such as <a href="/wiki/Yan%27an" title="Yan'an">Yan'an</a> (the CPC headquarter for much of the war).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199295_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199295-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The KMT's successes were hollow; the CPC had tactically withdrawn from the cities, and instead attacked KMT authorities by instigating protests amongst students and intellectuals in the cities (the KMT responded to these events with heavy-handed repression).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199296_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199296-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In the meantime, the KMT was struggling with factional infighting and Chiang Kai-shek's autocratic control over the party, which weakened the KMT's ability to respond to attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199296_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199296-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The third stage, lasting from July 1947 to August 1948, saw a limited counteroffensive by the CPC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199296_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199296-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The objective was to clear "Central China, strengthening North China, and recovering Northeast China."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199696_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199696-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> This policy, coupled with desertions from the KMT military force (by spring 1948 KMT military had lost an estimated 2 million troops, having 1 million troops left) and the increasing unpopularity of KMT rule.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199296_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199296-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The result was that the CPC was able to cut off KMT garrisons in <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> and retake several lost territories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199696_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199696-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The last stage, lasting from September 1948 to December 1949, saw the communist take the initiative and the collapse of KMT rule in mainland China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199696_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199696-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 October 1949, Mao declared the establishment of the PRC, which signified the end of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">Chinese Revolution</a> (as it is officially described by the CPC).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199696_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199696-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruling_party_.281949.E2.80.93present.29">Ruling party (1949–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ruling party (1949–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Chinese Revolution, directed by <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> and the CPC, led to the establishment of the (PRC) in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung199296_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung199296-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The PRC was founded on Marxist–Leninist principles, or more precisely, the sinification of Marxism–Leninism (officially known as Mao Zedong Thought, referred to in the West as Maoism).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeung1992407_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeung1992407-29"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1960s and 1970s, the CPC experienced a significant <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">ideological separation</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKornbergFaust2005103_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKornbergFaust2005103-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> By that time, Mao had begun saying that the "continued revolution under the <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">dictatorship of the proletariat</a>" stipulated that class enemies continued to exist even though the socialist revolution seemed to be complete, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWong2005131_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWong2005131-31"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin_birthday2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Stalin_birthday2.jpg/210px-Stalin_birthday2.jpg" width="210" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Stalin_birthday2.jpg/315px-Stalin_birthday2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Stalin_birthday2.jpg/420px-Stalin_birthday2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="557" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stalin_birthday2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chinese communists celebrate <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>'s birthday, 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following Mao's death in 1976, a power struggle between CPC General Secretary <a href="/wiki/Hua_Guofeng" title="Hua Guofeng">Hua Guofeng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> erupted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWong200547_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWong200547-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Deng won the struggle, and became the "paramount leader".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWong200547_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWong200547-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Deng, alongside <a href="/wiki/Chen_Yun" title="Chen Yun">Chen Yun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li_Xiannian" title="Li Xiannian">Li Xiannian</a>, spearheaded the <a href="/wiki/Reform_and_opening" title="Reform and opening" class="mw-redirect">Reform and opening</a> policy, and introduced the ideological concept of <a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_Chinese_characteristics" title="Socialism with Chinese characteristics">socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012254_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012254-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> In reversing some of Mao's "leftist" policies, Deng argued that a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a> could use the <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> without itself being <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-marketvsplanning_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketvsplanning-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> While asserting the political power of the Party, the change in policy generated significant economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-XinhuaCPChistory_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XinhuaCPChistory-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The new ideology, however, was contested on both sides of the spectrum, by Maoists as well as by those supporting political liberalization. With other social factors, the conflicts culminated in the <a href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_Protests" title="1989 Tiananmen Square Protests" class="mw-redirect">1989 Tiananmen Square Protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan201225_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan201225-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Deng's vision on economics prevailed, and by the early 1990s the concept a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_market_economy" title="Socialist market economy">socialist market economy</a> had been introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1997, Deng's beliefs (Deng Xiaoping Theory), were embedded in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Constitution of the Communist Party of China">CPC constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>CPC General Secretary <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Zemin" title="Jiang Zemin">Jiang Zemin</a> succeeded Deng as “paramount leader” in the 1990s, and continued most of his policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012100_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012100-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> As part of Jiang Zemin's nominal legacy, the CPC ratified the <a href="/wiki/Three_Represents" title="Three Represents">Three Represents</a> for the 2003 revision of the Party constitution, as a "guiding ideology" to encourage the Party to represent "advanced productive forces, the progressive course of China's culture, and the fundamental interests of the people."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012238_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012238-39"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The theory has legitimized the entry of private business owners and <a href="/wiki/Bourgeois" title="Bourgeois" class="mw-redirect">bourgeois</a> elements into the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012238_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012238-39"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a>, Jiang Zemin's successor as paramount leader, took office in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012317_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012317-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike Mao, Deng and Jiang Zemin, Hu laid emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Collective_leadership" title="Collective leadership">collective leadership</a> and opposed one-man dominance of the political system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012317_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012317-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The insistence on focusing on economic growth has led to a <a href="/wiki/Social_issues_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Social issues in the People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">wide range of serious social problems</a>. To address these, Hu introduced two main ideological concepts: the Scientific Outlook on Development and <a href="/wiki/Harmonious_Socialist_Society" title="Harmonious Socialist Society" class="mw-redirect">Harmonious Socialist Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012329_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012329-41"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Hu resigned from his post as CPC General Secretary and Chairman of the CMC at the <a href="/wiki/18th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="18th National Congress of the Communist Party of China">18th National Congress</a> held in 2012, and was succeeded in both posts by Xi Jinping.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Since taking power Xi has initiated the most concerted anti-corruption effort in decades, while centralizing powers in the office of CPC General Secretary at the expense of the collective leadership which has led foreign commentators to liken him to Mao.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="vertical-navbox vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:21.0em;">
