<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collective_leadership">Collective leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Collective leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Currently, in a bid to curtail the powers of the individual, <a href="/wiki/Collective_leadership" title="Collective leadership">collective leadership</a>, the idea that decisions will be taken through consensus, has become the ideal in the CPC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The concept has its origins back to <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> and the Russian Bolshevik Party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaylis1989102_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaylis1989102-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> At the level of the central party leadership this means that, for instance, all members of the Politburo Standing Committee are of equal standing (each member having only one vote).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> A member of the Politburo Standing Committee often represents a sector; during Mao's reign, he controlled the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kang_Sheng" title="Kang Sheng">Kang Sheng</a>, the security apparatus, and Zhou Enlai, the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_China" title="State Council of China" class="mw-redirect">State Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(China)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (China)" class="mw-redirect">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> This counts as informal power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, in a paradoxical relation, members of a body are ranked <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy" title="Hierarchy">hierarchically</a> (despite the fact that members are in theory equal to each others).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> In spite of this, the CPC is led by an informal leader principle, each collective leadership is led by a core, that is a paramount leader; a person who holds the offices of CPC General Secretary, CMC chairman and President of the PRC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger200222.E2.80.9324_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger200222.E2.80.9324-46"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Before Jiang Zemin's tenure as paramount leader, the party core and collective leadership were indistinguishable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In practice, the core was not responsible to the collective leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> However, by the time of Jiang, the party had begun propagating a responsibility system, referring to it in official pronouncements to the "core of the collective leadership".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnger2002158-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Democratic_centralism">Democratic centralism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Democratic centralism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_centralism" title="Democratic centralism">Democratic centralism</a></div>
<p>The CPC's organizational principle is democratic centralism, which is based on two principles; <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> (synonymous in official discourse with "socialist democracy" and "inner-party democracy") and <a href="/wiki/Centralism" title="Centralism" class="mw-redirect">centralism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> This has been the guiding organizational principle of the party since the <a href="/w/index.php?title=5th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="5th National Congress of the Communist Party of China (page does not exist)">5th National Congress</a>, held in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> In the words of the party constitution, "The Party is an integral body organized under its program and constitution and on the basis of democratic centralism".<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao once quipped that democratic centralism was "at once <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centralism" title="Centralism" class="mw-redirect">centralized</a>, with the two seeming opposites of democracy and centralization united in a definite form." Mao claimed that the superiority of democratic centralism laid in its internal contradictions, between democracy and centralism, and <a href="/wiki/Liberty" title="Liberty">freedom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discipline" title="Discipline">discipline</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, the CPC is claiming that "democracy is the lifeline of the Party, the lifeline of socialism".<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> But for democracy to be implemented, and functioning properly, there needs to be centralization.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Democracy in any form, the CPC claims, needs centralism, since without centralism there will be no order.<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Mao, democratic centralism "is centralized on the basis of democracy and democratic under centralized guidance. This is the only system that can give full expression to democracy with full powers vested in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=People%27s_congress&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="People's congress (page does not exist)">people's congresses</a> at all levels and, at the same time, guarantee centralized administration with the governments at each level exercising centralized management of all the affairs entrusted to them by the people’s congresses at the corresponding level and safeguarding whatever is essential to the democratic life of the people".<sup id="cite_ref-DemocraticcentralismQiushi_48-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DemocraticcentralismQiushi-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multi-party_Cooperation_System">Multi-party Cooperation System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Multi-party Cooperation System">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Multi-party_Cooperation_and_Political_Consultation_System&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Multi-party Cooperation and Political Consultation System (page does not exist)">Multi-party Cooperation and Political Consultation System</a> is led by the CPC in cooperation and consultation with the 8 parties which make up the United Front.<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Consultation takes place under the leadership of the CPC, with mass organizations, the United Front parties, and "representatives from all walks of life".<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> These consultations contribute, at least in theory, to the formation of the country's basic policy in the fields of political, economic, cultural and social affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC's relationship with other parties is based on the principle of "long-term coexistence and mutual supervision, treating each other with full sincerity and sharing weal or woe."<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> This process is institutionalized in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Political_Consultative_Conference" title="Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference">Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference</a> (CPPCC).<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> All the parties in the United Front support China's road to socialism, and hold steadfast to the leadership of the CPC.<sup id="cite_ref-multipartycooperationsystem_49-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multipartycooperationsystem-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite all this, the CPPCC is a body without any real power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200170_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200170-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> While discussions do take place, they are all supervised by the CPC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200170_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200170-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Organization of the Communist Party of China">Organization of the Communist Party of China</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_organization">Central organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Central organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="National Congress of the Communist Party of China">National Congress</a> is the party's highest body, and, since the <a href="/wiki/9th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="9th National Congress of the Communist Party of China">9th National Congress</a> in 1969, has been convened every five years (prior to the 9th Congress they were convened on an irregular basis). According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Constitution of the Communist Party of China">party's constitution</a>, a congress may not be postponed except "under extraordinary circumstances."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001228_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001228-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The party constitution gives the National Congress six responsibilities:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>electing the <a href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">Central Committee</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>electing the <a href="/wiki/Central_Commission_for_Discipline_Inspection" title="Central Commission for Discipline Inspection">Central Commission for Discipline Inspection</a> (CCDI);<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>examining the report of the outgoing Central Committee;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>examining the report of the outgoing CCDI;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>discussing and enacting party policies; and:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>revising the party's constitution.:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ol>
<p>In practice, the delegates rarely discuss issues at length at the National Congresses. Most substantive discussion takes place before the congress, in the preparation period, among a group of top party leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229_52-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001229-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In between National Congresses, the Central Committee is the highest decision-making institution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200166_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200166-53"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The CCDI is responsible for supervising party's internal anti-corruption and ethics system.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010394_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010394-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In between congresses the CCDI is under the authority of the Central Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010394_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010394-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Central Committee, as the party's highest decision-making institution between national congresses, elects several bodies to carry out its work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiu201141_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiu201141-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The 1st Plenary Session of a newly elected central committee elects the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of China">General Secretary</a> of the Central Committee, the party's titular leader, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Military_Commission_(China)" title="Central Military Commission (China)">Central Military Commission</a> (CMC), the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo of the Communist Party of China">Politburo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Politburo Standing Committee of the Communist Party of China">Politburo Standing Committee</a> (PSC), and since 2013, the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Commission_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="National Security Commission of the Communist Party of China">Central National Security Commission</a> (CNSC). The first plenum also endorses the composition of the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Secretariat of the Communist Party of China">Secretariat</a> and the leadership of the CCDI.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiu201141_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiu201141-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the party constitution, the General Secretary must be a member of the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee" title="Politburo Standing Committee" class="mw-redirect">Politburo Standing Committee</a> (PSC), and is responsible for convening meetings of the PSC and the Politburo, while also presiding over the work of the Secretariat.<sup id="cite_ref-CRI_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRI-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> The Politburo "exercises the functions and powers of the Central Committee when a plenum is not in session".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200185_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200185-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The PSC is the party's highest decision-making institution when the Politburo, the Central Committee and the National Congress are not in session.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller20117_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller20117-58"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> It convenes at least once a week.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010169_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph2010169-59"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> It was established at the 8th National Congress, in 1958, to take over the policy-making role formerly assumed by the Secretariat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELi200964_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELi200964-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The Secretariat is the top implementation body of the Central Committee, and can make decisions within the policy framework established by the Politburo; it is also responsible for supervising the work of organizations that report directly into the Central Committee, for example departments, commissions, publications, and so on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFu1993201_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFu1993201-61"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The CMC is the highest decision-making institution on military affairs within the party, and controls the operations of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The General Secretary has, since <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Zemin" title="Jiang Zemin">Jiang Zemin</a>, also served as Chairman of the CMC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike the <a href="/wiki/Collective_leadership" title="Collective leadership">collective leadership</a> ideal of other party organs, the CMC Chairman acts as <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> with full authority to appoint or dismiss top military officers at will.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson200174-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The CNSC "co-ordinates security strategies across various departments, including intelligence, the military, foreign affairs and the police in order to cope with growing challenges to stability at home and abroad."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCCNSC_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCNSC-63"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The General Secretary serves as the Chairman of the CNSC.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJNCSC_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJNCSC-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A first plenum of the Central Committee also elects several departments, bureaus, central leading groups and other institutions to pursue its work during a term (a "term" being the period elapsing between national congresses, usually five years).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001228_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackerrasMcMillenWatson2001228-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/General_Office_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Office of the Communist Party of China">General Office</a> is the party's "nerve centre", in charge of day-to-day administrative work, including communications, protocol, and setting agendas for meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012212_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012212-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC currently has four main central departments: the <a href="/wiki/Organization_Department_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Organization Department of the Communist Party of China">Organization Department</a>, responsible for overseeing provincial appointments and vetting cadres for future appointments,<sup id="cite_ref-COD_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COD-66"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Publicity_Department_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Publicity Department of the Communist Party of China">Publicity Department</a> (formerly "Propaganda Department"), which oversees the media and formulates the party line to the media,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGregor201217_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGregor201217-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuo2012123_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuo2012123-68"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/International_Department_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="International Department of the Communist Party of China" class="mw-redirect">International Department</a>, functioning as the party's "foreign affairs ministry" with other parties,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithWest2012127_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithWest2012127-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Front_Work_Department" title="United Front Work Department">United Front Work Department</a>, which oversees work with the country's non-Communist parties and other mass organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGregor201217_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGregor201217-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The CC also has direct control over the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Policy_Research_Office_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Central Policy Research Office of the Communist Party of China (page does not exist)">Central Policy Research Office</a>, which is responsible for researching issues of significant interest to the party leadership,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFiner200343_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFiner200343-70"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Central_Party_School_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Central Party School of the Communist Party of China">Central Party School</a>, which provides political training and ideological indoctrination in communist thought for high-ranking and rising cadres,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan201249_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan201249-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_History_Research_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Party History Research Centre (page does not exist)">Party History Research Centre</a>, which sets priorities for scholarly research in state-run universities and the Central Party School,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChambers200237_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChambers200237-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Compilation_and_Translation_Bureau" title="Compilation and Translation Bureau">Compilation and Translation Bureau</a>, which studies and translates the classical works of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYu2010viii_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYu2010viii-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The party's newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People's Daily">People's Daily</a></i>, is under the direct control of the Central Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELatham2007124_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELatham2007124-74"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The theoretical magazines <i><a href="/wiki/Qiushi" title="Qiushi">Seeking Truth from Facts</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Study_Times_(China)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Study Times (China) (page does not exist)">Study Times</a></i> are published by the Central Party School.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan201249_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan201249-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The various offices of the "Central Leading Groups", such as the Hong Kong and Macau Affairs Office, the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Affairs_Office" title="Taiwan Affairs Office">Taiwan Affairs Office</a>, and the Central Finance Office, also report to the central committee during a plenary session.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeath2014141_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeath2014141-75"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lower-level_organizations">Lower-level organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Lower-level organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Party committees exist at the level of <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_China" title="Provinces of China">provinces</a>; <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_China" title="Autonomous regions of China">autonomous regions</a>; <a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipalities_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipalities of China">municipalities directly under the central government</a>; <a href="//zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E8%AE%BE%E5%8C%BA%E7%9A%84%E5%B8%82" class="extiw" title="zh:设区的市">cities divided into districts</a>; <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_prefectures_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Autonomous prefectures of the People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">autonomous prefectures</a>; <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Counties of the People's Republic of China">counties</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Banners_of_Inner_Mongolia" title="Banners of Inner Mongolia">banners</a>); <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_counties_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Autonomous counties of the People's Republic of China">autonomous counties</a>; <a href="//zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E4%B8%8D%E8%AE%BE%E5%8C%BA%E7%9A%84%E5%B8%82" class="extiw" title="zh:不设区的市">cities not divided into districts</a>; and <a href="/wiki/District_(China)#City-controlled_districts" title="District (China)">municipal districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> These committees are elected by party congresses (at their own level).<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Local party congresses are supposed to be held every fifth year, but under extraordinary circumstances they may be held earlier or postponed. However that decision must be approved by the next higher level of the local party committee.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The number of delegates and the procedures for their election are decided by the local party committee, but must also have the approval of the next higher party committee.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A local party congress has many of the same duties as the National Congress, and it is responsible for examining the report of the local Party Committee at the corresponding level; examining the report of the local Commission for Discipline Inspection at the corresponding level; discussing and adopting resolutions on major issues in the given area; and electing the local Party Committee and the local Commission for Discipline Inspection at the corresponding level.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Party committees of "a province, autonomous region, municipality directly under the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_China" title="Government of China">central government</a>, city divided into districts, or autonomous prefecture [are] elected for a term of five years", and include full and alternate members.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The party committees "of a county (banner), autonomous county, city not divided into districts, or municipal district [are] elected for a term of five years", but full and alternate members "must have a Party standing of three years or more."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> If a local Party Congress is held before or after the given date, the term of the members of the Party Committee shall be correspondingly shortened or lengthened.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A local Party Committee is responsible to the Party Committee at the next higher level.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The number of full and alternate members at the local Party Committee is decided by the Party Committee at the next higher level.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Vacancies in a Party Committee shall be filled by an alternate members according to the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_precedence" title="Order of precedence">order of precedence</a>, which is decided by the number of votes an alternate member got during his or hers election.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> A Party Committee must convene for at least two plenary meetings a year.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> During its tenure, a Party Committee shall "carry out the directives of the next higher Party organizations and the resolutions of the Party congresses at the corresponding levels."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The local Standing Committee (analogous to the Central Politburo) is elected at the first plenum of the corresponding Party Committee after the local party congress.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> A Standing Committee is responsible to the Party Committee at the corresponding level and the Party Committee at the next higher level.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> A Standing Committee exercises the duties and responsibilities of the corresponding Party Committee when it is not in session.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: ivory;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It is my will to join the Communist Party of China, uphold the Party's program, observe the provisions of the Party constitution, fulfill a Party member's duties, carry out the Party's decisions, strictly observe Party discipline, guard Party secrets, be loyal to the Party, work hard, fight for communism throughout my life, be ready at all times to sacrifice my all for the Party and the people, and never betray the Party."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>—Communist Party admission oath.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>To join the party, an applicant must be 18 years of age, and must spend a year as a probationary member.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In contrast to the past, when emphasis was placed on the applicants' ideological criteria, the current CPC stresses technical and educational qualifications.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> To become a probationary member, the applicant must take an admission oath before the party flag.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The relevant CPC organization is responsible for observing and educating probationary members.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Probationary members have duties similar to those of full members, with the exception that they may not vote in party elections nor stand for election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Many join the CPC through the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Youth_League_of_China" title="Communist Youth League of China">Communist Youth League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Under Jiang Zemin, private entrepreneurs were allowed to become party members.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183_77-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2012183-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the CPC constitution, a member, in short, must follow orders, be disciplined, uphold unity, serve the Party and the people, and promote the socialist way of life.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Members enjoy the privilege of attending Party meetings, reading relevant Party documents, receiving Party education, participating in Party discussions through the Party's newspapers and journals, making suggestions and proposal, making "well-grounded criticism of any Party organization or member at Party meetings" (even of the central party leadership), voting and standing for election, and of opposing and criticizing Party resolutions ("provided that they resolutely carry out the resolution or policy while it is in force"); and they have the ability "to put forward any request, appeal, or complaint to higher Party organizations, even up to the Central Committee, and ask the organizations concerned for a responsible reply."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> No party organization, including the CPC central leadership, can deprive a member of these rights.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 30 June 2015, individuals who identify as farmers, herdsmen and fishermen make up 25.9 million members; members identifying as workers totalled 7,3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCmembersoccupation_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCmembersoccupation-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Another group, the "Managing, professional and technical staff in enterprises and public institutions", made up 12,5 million, 9 million identified as working in administrative staff and 7,4 million described themselves as party cadres.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCmembersoccupation_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCmembersoccupation-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> 21,7 million women are CPC members.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCmembersoccupation_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCmembersoccupation-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC currently has 87.79 million members,<sup id="cite_ref-CPCmembersoccupation_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCmembersoccupation-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> making it the second largest political party in the world after India's <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communist_Youth_League">Communist Youth League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Communist Youth League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communist_Youth_League_of_China" title="Communist Youth League of China">Communist Youth League of China</a></div>
<p>The Communist Youth League (CYL) is the CPC's <a href="/wiki/Youth_wing" title="Youth wing">youth wing</a>, and the largest mass organization for youth in China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the CPC's constitution the CYL is a "mass organization of advanced young people under the leadership of the Communist Party of China; it functions as a party school where a large number of young people learn about socialism with Chinese characteristics and about communism through practice; it is the Party's assistant and reserve force."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> To join, an applicant has to be between the ages of 14 and 28.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> It controls and supervises <a href="/wiki/Young_Pioneers_of_China" title="Young Pioneers of China">Young Pioneers</a>, a youth organization for children below the age of 14.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2007582-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The organizational structure of CYL is an exact copy of the CPC's; the highest body is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Youth_League_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Congress of the Communist Youth League of China (page does not exist)">National Congress</a>, followed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Youth_League_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Central Committee of the Communist Youth League of China (page does not exist)">Central Committee</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Politburo_of_the_Communist_Youth_League_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Politburo of the Communist Youth League of China (page does not exist)">Politburo</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Communist_Youth_League_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Politburo Standing Committee of the Communist Youth League of China (page does not exist)">Politburo Standing Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2007583_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2007583-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the Central Committee (and all central organs) of the CYL work under the guidance of the CPC central leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Therefore, in a peculiar situation, CYL bodies are both responsible to higher bodies within CYL and the CPC, a distinct organization.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=17th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Youth_League&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="17th National Congress of the Communist Youth League (page does not exist)">17th National Congress</a> (held in 2013), CYL has 89 million members.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the Article 53 of the CPC constitution, "the Party emblem and flag are the symbol and sign of the Communist Party of China."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCactualconstitution_76-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCactualconstitution-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> At the beginning of its history, the CPC did not have a single official standard for the flag, but instead allowed individual party committees to copy the flag of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCemblemflag_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCemblemflag-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> On 28 April 1942, the Central Politburo decreed the establishment of a sole official flag. "The flag of the CPC has the length-to-width proportion of 3:2 with a <a href="/wiki/Hammer_and_sickle" title="Hammer and sickle">hammer and sickle</a> in the upper-left corner, and with no five-pointed star. The Political Bureau authorizes the General Office to custom-make a number of standard flags and distribute them to all major organs".<sup id="cite_ref-CPCemblemflag_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCemblemflag-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People's Daily">People's Daily</a></i>, "The standard party flag is 120&#160;centimeters (cm) in length and 80&#160;cm in width. In the center of the upper-left corner (a quarter of the length and width to the border) is a yellow hammer-and-sickle 30&#160;cm in diameter. The flag sleeve (pole hem) is in white and 6.5&#160;cm in width. The dimension of the pole hem is not included in the measure of the flag. The red color symbolizes revolution; the hammer-and-sickle are tools of workers and peasants, meaning that the Communist Party of China represents the interests of the masses and the people; the yellow color signifies brightness."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCemblemflag_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCemblemflag-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In total the flag has five dimensions, the sizes are "no. 1: 388&#160;cm in length and 192&#160;cm in width; no. 2: 240&#160;cm in length and 160&#160;cm in width; no. 3: 192&#160;cm in length and 128&#160;cm in width; no. 4: 144&#160;cm in length and 96&#160;cm in width; no. 5: 96&#160;cm in length and 64&#160;cm in width."<sup id="cite_ref-CPCemblemflag_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCemblemflag-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> On 21 September 1966, the <a href="/wiki/General_Office_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="General Office of the Communist Party of China">CPC General Office</a> issued "Regulations on the Production and Use of the CPC Flag and Emblem", which stated that the emblem and flag were the official symbols and signs of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-CPCemblemflag_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPCemblemflag-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology">Ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ideology_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="Ideology of the Communist Party of China">Ideology of the Communist Party of China</a></div>
<p>It has been argued in recent years, mainly by foreign commentators, that the CPC does not have an ideology, and that the party organization is <a href="/wiki/Pragmatism" title="Pragmatism">pragmatic</a> and interested only in what works.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown201252_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown201252-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> This view is considered wrong by some in many ways, since official statements make it very clear the party does have a coherent worldview.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown201252_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown201252-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jintao" title="Hu Jintao">Hu Jintao</a> stated in 2012 that the Western world is "threatening to divide us" and that "the international culture of the West is strong while we are weak ... Ideological and cultural fields are our main targets".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown201252_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown201252-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC puts a great deal of effort into the party schools and into crafting its ideological message.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown201252_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown201252-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Before the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Practice_Is_the_Sole_Criterion_for_the_Truth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Practice Is the Sole Criterion for the Truth (page does not exist)">Practice Is the Sole Criterion for the Truth</a>" campaign, the relationship between ideology and decision-making was a deductive one, meaning that policy-making was derived from ideological knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Under Deng this relationship was turned upside down, with decision-making justifying ideology and not the other way around.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Lastly, Chinese policy-makers believe that one of the reasons for the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> was <a href="/wiki/State_ideology_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="State ideology of the Soviet Union" class="mw-redirect">its stagnant state ideology</a>. They therefore believe that their party ideology must be dynamic to safeguard the party's rule, unlike the Soviet Union's communist party, whose ideology they believe became "rigid, unimaginative, ossified, and disconnected from reality."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008105-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_ideology">Formal ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Formal ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: ivory;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I am a Marxist. The essence of Marxism is change, [...] <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> by stressing change. The Marxist in China today is not a stubborn, dogmatic, and outdated 19th-century old man, but a dynamic, pro-change, young thinker. We have a flexible approach: if <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marx</a>'s words are still applicable, we will use them; for things he did not articulate clearly, we will spell them out; for what he did not say, we will boldly come up with something new."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>—<a href="/wiki/Ye_Xiaowen" title="Ye Xiaowen">Ye Xiaowen</a> on the role of Marxist thought.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011369_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011369-85"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxism–Leninism</a> was the first official ideology of the Communist Party of China.<sup id="cite_ref-MLT_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLT-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the CPC, "Marxism–Leninism reveals the <a href="/wiki/Historical_materialism" title="Historical materialism">universal laws governing the development of history of human society</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-MLT_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLT-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> To the CPC, Marxism–Leninism provides a "vision of the <a href="/wiki/Capitalist_mode_of_production_(Marxist_theory)" title="Capitalist mode of production (Marxist theory)">contradictions in capitalist society</a> and of the inevitability of a future socialist and communist societies".<sup id="cite_ref-MLT_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLT-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Daily" title="People's Daily">People's Daily</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong_Thought" title="Mao Zedong Thought" class="mw-redirect">Mao Zedong Thought</a> "is Marxism–Leninism applied and developed in China".<sup id="cite_ref-MLT_86-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLT-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Mao Zedong Thought was conceived not only by <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a>, but by leading party officials.<sup id="cite_ref-MaoZedongThought_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MaoZedongThought-87"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg/220px-Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg" width="220" height="355" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg/330px-Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg/440px-Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="897" data-file-height="1449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marx_et_Engels_%C3%A0_Shanghai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A monument dedicated to Marx (left) and Engels (right) in Shanghai, China</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While non-Chinese analysts generally agree that the CPC has rejected orthodox Marxism–Leninism and Mao Zedong Thought (or at least basic thoughts within orthodox thinking), the CPC itself disagrees.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008104_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008104-88"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Certain groups argue that Jiang Zemin ended the CPC's formal commitment to Marxism with the introduction of the ideological theory, the <a href="/wiki/Three_Represents" title="Three Represents">Three Represents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn201199_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn201199-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> However, party theorist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leng_Rong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leng Rong (page does not exist)">Leng Rong</a> disagrees, claiming that "President Jiang rid the Party of the ideological obstacles to different kinds of ownership [...] He did not give up Marxism or socialism. He strengthened the Party by providing a modern understanding of Marxism and socialism—which is why we talk about a ‘socialist market economy’ with Chinese characteristics."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn201199_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn201199-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The attainment of true "communism" is still described as the CPC's and China's "ultimate goal".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> While the CPC claims that China is in the <a href="/wiki/Primary_stage_of_socialism" title="Primary stage of socialism">primary stage of socialism</a>, party theorists argue that the current development stage "looks a lot like capitalism".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Alternately, certain party theorists argue that “capitalism is the early or first stage of communism.”<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Some have dismissed the concept of a primary stage of socialism as intellectual cynicism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lawrence_Kuhn" title="Robert Lawrence Kuhn">Robert Lawrence Kuhn</a>, a China analyst, "When I first heard this rationale, I thought it more comic than clever—a wry caricature of hack propagandists leaked by intellectual cynics. But the 100-year horizon comes from serious political theorists".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527_90-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011527-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping_Theory" title="Deng Xiaoping Theory">Deng Xiaoping Theory</a> was added to the party constitution at the 14th National Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The concepts of "<a href="/wiki/Socialism_with_Chinese_characteristics" title="Socialism with Chinese characteristics">socialism with Chinese characteristics</a>" and "the <a href="/wiki/Primary_stage_of_socialism" title="Primary stage of socialism">primary stage of socialism</a>" were credited to the theory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011684-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Deng Xiaoping Theory can be defined as a belief that <a href="/wiki/State_socialism" title="State socialism">state socialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">state planning</a> is not by definition communist, and that market mechanisms are class neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011668_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011668-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the party needs to react to the changing situation dynamically; to know if a certain policy is obsolete or not, the party had to "<a href="/wiki/Seek_truth_from_facts" title="Seek truth from facts">seek truth from facts</a>" and follow the slogan "practice is the sole criterion for the truth".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChan2003180_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChan2003180-92"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 14th National Congress, Jiang reiterated Deng's mantra that it was unnecessary to ask if something was socialist or capitalist, since the important factor was whether it worked.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011685_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011685-93"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Three_Represents" title="Three Represents">Three Represents</a>", literally a Marxism adapted to Chinese conditions, was adopted by the party at the 16th National Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChan2003201_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChan2003201-94"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Certain segments within the CPC criticized the Three Represents as being un-Marxist and a betrayal of basic Marxist values, supporters viewed it as a further development of socialism with Chinese characteristics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011108.E2.80.93109_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011108.E2.80.93109-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Jiang disagreed, and had concluded that attaining the communist mode of production, as formulated by earlier communists, was more complex than had been realized, and that it was useless to try to force a change in the mode of production, as it had to develop naturally, by following the <a href="/wiki/Historical_materialism" title="Historical materialism">economic laws of history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011107.E2.80.93108_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011107.E2.80.93108-96"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The theory is most notable for allowing capitalists, officially referred to as the "new social strata", to join the party on the grounds that they engaged in "honest labor and work" and through their labour contributed "to build[ing] socialism with Chinese characteristics."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011110_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuhn2011110-97"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The 3rd Plenary Session of the <a href="/wiki/16th_Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="16th Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">16th Central Committee</a> conceived and formulated the ideology of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Outlook_on_Development" title="Scientific Outlook on Development">Scientific Outlook on Development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIzuhara2013110_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIzuhara2013110-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> It is considered to be Hu Jintao's contribution to the official ideological discourse.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuoGuo2008119_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuoGuo2008119-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> To apply the Scientific Outlook on Development to Chinese conditions, the CPC must adhere to building a <a href="/wiki/Harmonious_Socialist_Society" title="Harmonious Socialist Society" class="mw-redirect">Harmonious Socialist Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuoGuo2008121_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuoGuo2008121-100"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Deng did not believe that the fundamental difference between the <a href="/wiki/Capitalist_mode_of_production_(Marxist_theory)" title="Capitalist mode of production (Marxist theory)">capitalist mode of production</a> and the socialist mode of production was <a href="/wiki/Central_planning" title="Central planning" class="mw-redirect">central planning</a> versus <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free markets</a>. He said, "A planned economy is not the definition of socialism, because there is planning under capitalism; the market economy happens under socialism, too. Planning and market forces are both ways of controlling economic activity".<sup id="cite_ref-marketvsplanning_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketvsplanning-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Jiang Zemin supported Deng's thinking, and stated in a party gathering that it did not matter if a certain mechanism was capitalist or socialist, because the only thing that mattered was whether it worked.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> It was at this gathering that Jiang Zemin introduced the term <a href="/wiki/Socialist_market_economy" title="Socialist market economy">socialist market economy</a>, which replaced <a href="/wiki/Chen_Yun" title="Chen Yun">Chen Yun</a>'s "planned socialist market economy".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVogel2011682-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In his report to the 14th National Congress Jiang Zemin told the delegates that the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a> would "let market forces play a basic role in resource allocation."<sup id="cite_ref-basicdecisive_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basicdecisive-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 15th National Congress, the party line was changed to "make market forces further play their role in resource allocation"; this line continued until the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Third_plenum_of_the_18th_Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Third plenum of the 18th Central Committee of the Communist Party of China (page does not exist)">3rd Plenary Session</a> of the <a href="/wiki/18th_Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="18th Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">18th Central Committee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-basicdecisive_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basicdecisive-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> when it was amended to "let market forces play a <i>decisive</i> role in <a href="/wiki/Resource_allocation" title="Resource allocation">resource allocation</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-basicdecisive_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basicdecisive-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, the 3rd Plenary Session of the 18th Central Committee upheld the creed "Maintain the dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> and strengthen the economic vitality of the <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprises" title="State-owned enterprises" class="mw-redirect">State-owned economy</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-basicdecisive_101-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basicdecisive-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: ivory;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"[...] their theory that capitalism is the ultimate has been shaken, and socialist development has experienced a miracle. Western capitalism has suffered reversals, a financial crisis, a credit crisis, a crisis of confidence, and their self-conviction has wavered. Western countries have begun to reflect, and openly or secretively compare themselves against China’s politics, economy and path."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"><cite>—<a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>, the CPC General Secretary, on the inevitability of socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>The CPC views the world as organized into two opposing camps; socialist and capitalist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> They insist that socialism, on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Historical_materialism" title="Historical materialism">historical materialism</a>, will eventually triumph over capitalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent years, when the party has been asked to explain the capitalist <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> occurring, the party has returned to the writings of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200762-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite admitting that globalization developed through the capitalist system, the party's leaders and theorist argue that globalization is not intrinsically capitalist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The reason being that if globalization was purely capitalist, it would exclude an alternate socialist form of modernity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Globalization, as with the <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, therefore does not have one specific class character (neither socialist or capitalist) according to the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The instance that globalization is not fixed in nature, comes from Deng's insistence that China can pursue socialist modernization by incorporating elements of capitalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200763-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of this there is considerable optimism within the CPC that despite the current capitalist dominance of globalization, globalization can be turned into a vehicle supporting socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200764_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeazleKnight200764-105"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Maoist_Communist_Party_(Turkey)" title="Maoist Communist Party (Turkey)">MKP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist_Communist_Party_(Turkey/Northern_Kurdistan)" title="Marxist–Leninist Communist Party (Turkey/Northern Kurdistan)">MLKP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Communist_Party_of_Turkey" title="Revolutionary Communist Party of Turkey">TDKP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Labour_Party_of_Turkey" title="Communist Labour Party of Turkey">TKEP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Labour_Party_of_Turkey/Leninist" title="Communist Labour Party of Turkey/Leninist">TKEP/L</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Workers_Party_of_Turkey" title="Communist Workers Party of Turkey">TKIP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Turkey/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" title="Communist Party of Turkey/Marxist–Leninist">TKP/ML</a></small></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Ukraine" title="Communist Party of Ukraine">Ukraine</a></li>
<li>United Kingdom
<ul>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Britain" title="Communist Party of Britain">CP</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Communist_Group_(UK)" title="Revolutionary Communist Group (UK)">RCG</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Great_Britain_(Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist)" title="Communist Party of Great Britain (Marxist–Leninist)">CPGB-ML</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/New_Communist_Party_of_Britain" title="New Communist Party of Britain">NCPB</a></small></li>
<li><small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Scotland" title="Communist Party of Scotland">CPS</a></small></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd><i>Former parties</i></dd>
