<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communist_parties">Communist parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Communist parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The CPC continues to have relations with non-ruling communist and workers' parties and attends international communist conferences, most notably the <a href="/wiki/International_Meeting_of_Communist_and_Workers%27_Parties" title="International Meeting of Communist and Workers' Parties">International Meeting of Communist and Workers' Parties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Delegates of foreign communist parties still visit China; in 2013, for instance, the General Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Communist_Party" title="Portuguese Communist Party">Portuguese Communist Party</a> (PCP), <a href="/wiki/Jeronimo_de_Sousa" title="Jeronimo de Sousa" class="mw-redirect">Jeronimo de Sousa</a>, personally met with <a href="/wiki/Liu_Qibao" title="Liu Qibao">Liu Qibao</a>, a member of the Central Politburo.<sup id="cite_ref-PCP_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCP-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> In another instance, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Laurent_(politician)" title="Pierre Laurent (politician)">Pierre Laurent</a>, the National Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/French_Communist_Party" title="French Communist Party">French Communist Party</a> (FCP), met with <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yunshan" title="Liu Yunshan">Liu Yunshan</a>, a Politburo Standing Committee member.<sup id="cite_ref-FCP_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCP-108"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014 Xi Jinping, the CPC General Secretary, personally met with <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Zyuganov" title="Gennady Zyuganov">Gennady Zyuganov</a>, the First Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Communist Party of the Russian Federation">Communist Party of the Russian Federation</a> (CPRF), to discuss party-to-party relations.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> While the CPC retains contact with major parties such as the PCP,<sup id="cite_ref-PCP_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCP-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> FCP,<sup id="cite_ref-FCP_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCP-108"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> the CPRF,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Communist Party of Bohemia and Moravia">Communist Party of Bohemia and Moravia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Brazil" title="Communist Party of Brazil">Communist Party of Brazil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Unified_Marxist%E2%88%92Leninist)" title="Communist Party of Nepal (Unified Marxist−Leninist)" class="mw-redirect">Communist Party of Nepal (Unified Marxist−Leninist)</a><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain" title="Communist Party of Spain">Communist Party of Spain</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> the party retains relations with minor communist and workers' parties, such as the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Australia" title="Communist Party of Australia">Communist Party of Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Workers_Party_of_Bangladesh" title="Workers Party of Bangladesh">Workers Party of Bangladesh</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Bangladesh_(Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist)_(Barua)" title="Communist Party of Bangladesh (Marxist–Leninist) (Barua)">Communist Party of Bangladesh (Marxist–Leninist) (Barua)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Communist Party of Sri Lanka">Communist Party of Sri Lanka</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Belgium" title="Workers' Party of Belgium">Workers' Party of Belgium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Workers%27_Party" title="Hungarian Workers' Party">Hungarian Workers' Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Workers%27_Party" title="Dominican Workers' Party">Dominican Workers' Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Party_for_the_Transformation_of_Honduras" title="Party for the Transformation of Honduras">Party for the Transformation of Honduras</a>, for instance.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In recent years, noting the self-reform of the European social democratic movement in the 1980s and 1990s, the CPC "has noted the increased marginalization of West European communist parties."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008100_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh2008100-117"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruling_parties_of_socialist_states">Ruling parties of socialist states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ruling parties of socialist states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The CPC has retained close relations with the remaining <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist states</a> still espousing communism: Cuba, Laos, North Korea and Vietnam and their respective ruling parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200881_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200881-118"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> It spends a fair amount of time analyzing the situation in the remaining socialist states, trying to reach conclusions as to why these states survived when so many did not, following the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">collapse of the Eastern European socialist states</a> in 1989 and the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> In general, the analyses of the remaining socialist states and their chances of survival have been positive, and the CPC believes that the socialist movement will be revitalized sometime in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The ruling party which the CPC is most interested in is the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Vietnam" title="Communist Party of Vietnam">Communist Party of Vietnam</a> (CPV).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> In general the CPV is considered a model example of socialist development in the post-Soviet era.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Chinese analysts on Vietnam believe that the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Doi_Moi" title="Doi Moi">Doi Moi</a> reform policy at the <a href="/wiki/6th_National_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Vietnam" title="6th National Congress of the Communist Party of Vietnam">6th CPV National Congress</a> is the key reason for Vietnam's current success.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While the CPC is probably the organization with most access to North Korea, writing about North Korea is tightly circumscribed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The few reports accessible to the general public are those about <a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Korean_economic_reforms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="North Korean economic reforms (page does not exist)">North Korean economic reforms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882_119-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> While Chinese analysts of North Korea tend to speak positively of North Korea in public, in official discussions they show much disdain for North Korea's economic system, the <a href="/wiki/North_Korea%27s_cult_of_personality" title="North Korea's cult of personality" class="mw-redirect">cult of personality</a> which pervades society, the <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim family</a>, the idea of hereditary succession in a socialist state, the security state, the use of scarce resources on the <a href="/wiki/Korean_People%27s_Army" title="Korean People's Army">Korean People's Army</a> and the general impoverishment of the North Korean people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882.E2.80.9383_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200882.E2.80.9383-121"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> There are those analysts who compare the current situation of North Korea with that of China during the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Over the years, the CPC has tried to persuade the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="Workers' Party of Korea">Workers' Party of Korea</a> (or WPK, North Korea's ruling party) to introduce economic reforms by showing them key economic infrastructure in China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, in 2006 the CPC invited the <a href="/wiki/First_Secretary_of_the_Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="First Secretary of the Workers' Party of Korea">WPK General Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_China_Plain" title="North China Plain">Guandong province</a> to showcase the success economic reforms have brought China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In general, the CPC considers the WPK and North Korea to be negative examples of a communist ruling party and socialist state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200883-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There is a considerable degree of interest in Cuba within the CPC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/First_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="First Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba">First Secretary of the Communist Party of Cuba</a> (PCC), is greatly admired, and books have been written focusing on the successes of the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884_120-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200884-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Communication between the CPC and the PCC has increased considerably since the 1990s, hardly a month going by without a diplomatic exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885-123"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 4th Plenary Session of the <a href="/wiki/16th_Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_China" title="16th Central Committee of the Communist Party of China">16th Central Committee</a>, which discussed the possibility of the CPC learning from other ruling parties, praise was heaped on the PCC.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885-123"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Wu_Guanzheng" title="Wu Guanzheng">Wu Guanzheng</a>, a Central Politburo member, met with Fidel Castro in 2007, he gave him a personal letter written by Hu Jintao: "Facts have shown that China and Cuba are trustworthy good friends, good comrades, and good brothers who treat each other with sincerity. The two countries' friendship has withstood the test of a changeable international situation, and the friendship has been further strengthened and consolidated."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885.E2.80.9386_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200885.E2.80.9386-124"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-communist_parties">Non-communist parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Non-communist parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the decline and fall of communism in Eastern Europe, the CPC has begun establishing party-to-party relations with non-communist parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmithWest2012127_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmithWest2012127-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> These relations are sought so that the CPC can learn from them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200886.E2.80.9392_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200886.E2.80.9392-125"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, the CPC has been eager to understand how the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party" title="People's Action Party">People's Action Party of Singapore</a> (PAP) maintains its total domination over Singaporean politics through its "low-key presence, but total control."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893-126"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the CPC's own analysis of Singapore, the PAP's dominance can be explained by its "well-developed social network, which controls constituencies effectively by extending its tentacles deeply into society through branches of government and party-controlled groups."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893-126"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> While the CPC accepts that Singapore is a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">democracy</a>, they view it as a <a href="/wiki/Guided_democracy" title="Guided democracy">guided democracy</a> led by the PAP.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200893-126"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Other differences are, according to the CPC, "that it is not a political party based on the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a>—instead it is a political party of the elite ... It is also a political party of the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a>, not a <a href="/wiki/Vanguard_party" title="Vanguard party" class="mw-redirect">revolutionary party</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200894_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200894-127"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Other parties the CPC studies and maintains strong party-to-party relations with are the <a href="/wiki/United_Malays_National_Organisation" title="United Malays National Organisation">United Malays National Organisation</a>, which has ruled Malaysia democratically since 1957, and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_(Japan)" title="Liberal Democratic Party (Japan)">Liberal Democratic Party</a> in Japan, which dominated Japanese politics for over five uninterrupted decades.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200895.E2.80.9396_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200895.E2.80.9396-128"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The CPC has, since Jiang Zemin's time, made friendly overtures to its erstwhile foe, the Kuomintang. The CPC emphasizes strong party-to-party relations with the KMT so as to strengthen the probability of the reunification of Taiwan with mainland China.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896-129"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> However, several studies have been written on the KMT's loss of power in 2000, after having ruled Taiwan since 1949 (the KMT officially ruled China from 1928 to 1949).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896-129"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In general, one-party states or dominant-party states are of special interest to the party, and party-to-party relations are formed so that the CPC can study them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200896-129"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, the longevity of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Syria_Region" title="Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party – Syria Region">Syrian Regional Branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ba%27ath_Party_(Syrian-dominated_faction)" title="Ba'ath Party (Syrian-dominated faction)">Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party</a> is attributed to the personalization of power in the <a href="/wiki/Al-Assad_family" title="Al-Assad family">al-Assad family</a>, the strong <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a>, the inheritance of power, which passed from <a href="/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad" title="Hafez al-Assad">Hafez al-Assad</a> to his son <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>, and the role given to the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_military" title="Syrian military" class="mw-redirect">Syrian military</a> in politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping,_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China,_y_de_su_esposa,_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_(8959188037).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg/220px-Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg/330px-Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg/440px-Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping%2C_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China%2C_y_de_su_esposa%2C_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_%288959188037%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2489" data-file-height="1557" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cena_de_Estado_que_en_honor_del_Excmo._Sr._Xi_Jinping,_Presidente_de_la_Rep%C3%BAblica_Popular_China,_y_de_su_esposa,_Sra._Peng_Liyuan_(8959188037).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Xi Jinping (second from left) with <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto" title="Enrique Peña Nieto">Enrique Peña Nieto</a> (second from right), the current <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">President of Mexico</a> and a leading member of the social democratic Institutional Revolutionary Party</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In recent years, the CPC has been especially interested in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> as shown by the increasing number of delegates sent to and received from these countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Of special fascination for the CPC is the 71-year-long rule of the <a href="/wiki/Institutional_Revolutionary_Party" title="Institutional Revolutionary Party">Institutional Revolutionary Party</a> (PRI) in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> While the CPC attributed the PRI's long reign in power to the strong presidential system, tapping into the <a href="/wiki/Machismo" title="Machismo">machismo</a> culture of the country, its nationalist posture, its close identification with the rural populace and the implementation of <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalization</a> alongside the <a href="/wiki/Marketization" title="Marketization">marketization</a> of the economy, <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> the CPC concluded that the PRI failed because of the lack of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Inner-party_democracy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Inner-party democracy (page does not exist)">inner-party democracy</a>, its pursuit of <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a>, its rigid party structures that could not be reformed, its <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">political corruption</a>, the pressure of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, and American interference in Mexican politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897_130-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200897-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> While the CPC was slow to recognize the <a href="/wiki/Pink_tide" title="Pink tide">Pink tide</a> in Latin America, it has strengthened party-to-party relations with several socialist and anti-American political parties over the years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC has occasionally expressed some irritation over <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Chavez" title="Hugo Chavez" class="mw-redirect">Hugo Chavez</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist" class="mw-redirect">anti-capitalist</a> and anti-American rhetoric.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, in 2013 the CPC reached an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/United_Socialist_Party_of_Venezuela" title="United Socialist Party of Venezuela">United Socialist Party of Venezuela</a> (PSUV), which was founded by Chavez, for the CPC to educate PSUV cadres in political and social fields.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> By 2008, the CPC claimed to have established relations with 99 political parties in 29 Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Social_democrat" title="Social democrat" class="mw-redirect">Social democratic</a> movements in Europe have been of great interest to the CPC since the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> With the exception of a short period in which the CPC forged party-to-party relations with <a href="/wiki/Far-right" title="Far-right" class="mw-redirect">far-right</a> parties during the 1970s in an effort to halt "<a href="/wiki/Soviet_imperialism" title="Soviet imperialism" class="mw-redirect">Soviet expansionism</a>", the CPC's relations with European social democratic parties were its first serious efforts to establish cordial party-to-party relations with non-communist parties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC credits the European social democrats with creating a "capitalism with a human face".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Before the 1980s, the CPC had a highly negative and dismissive view of social democracy, a view dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinist</a> view on the social democratic movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> By the 1980s that view had changed, and the CPC concluded that it could actually learn something from the social democratic movement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898_131-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200898-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> CPC delegates were sent all over Europe to observe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899-133"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> It should be noted that by the 1980s most European social democratic parties were facing electoral decline, and were in a period of self-reform.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899-133"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC followed this with great interest, laying most weight on reform efforts within the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">British Labour Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899-133"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The CPC concluded that both parties were re-elected because they modernized, replacing traditional <a href="/wiki/State_socialism" title="State socialism">state socialist tenets</a> with new ones supporting <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a>, shedding the belief in <a href="/wiki/Big_government" title="Big government">big government</a>, conceiving a new view of the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>, changing negative views of the market, and moving from their traditional support base of <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> to entrepreneurs, younger members and students.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899.E2.80.93100_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShambaugh200899.E2.80.93100-134"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Communist_Party_of_China&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEGao2009119-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGao2009119_10-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGao2009">Gao 2009</a>, p.&#160;119.</span></li>

Cambridge University Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521587379" title="Special:BookSources/0521587379">0521587379</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACommunist+Party+of+China&amp;rft.au=White%2C+Stephen&amp;rft.btitle=Russia%27s+New+Politics%3A+The+Management+of+a+Postcommunist+Society&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0521587379&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
